tony whitlock richard cook city council ____________ shawn m bell city administrator ____________ cd rhodes iii city attorney ____________ teresa benjamin city clerk preface this a recodification of the general and permanent ordinances of lake city south carolina source materials used in the preparation of the the 1983 ordinances subsequently adopted by the city council the source of each section is included in the history note appearing in parentheses at the end thereof the absence of such a note indicates that the section is new and was adopted for the first time with the adoption of the use of the comparative tables appearing in the back of this the reader can locate any section of the 1983 any subsequent ordinance included herein the chapters of the been conveniently arranged in alphabetical order and the various sections within each chapter have been provided catchlines to facilitate usage notes which tie related sections of the which refer to relevant state law have been included a table listing the state law citations and setting forth their location within the included at the back of this system the chapter and section numbering system used in this the same system used in many state and local government codes each section number consists of two parts separated by a dash the figure before the dash refers to the chapter number and the figure after the dash refers to the position of the section within the chapter thus the second section of chapter 1 is numbered 12 and the first section of chapter 6 is 61 under this system each section is identified with its chapter and at the same time new sections can be inserted in their proper place by using the decimal system for amendments for example if new material consisting of one section that would logically come between sections 61 and 62 is desired to be added such new section would be numbered 615 new articles and new divisions may be included in the same way or in the case of articles may be placed at the end of the chapter embracing the subject and in the case of divisions may be placed at the end of the article embracing the subject the next successive number shall be assigned to the new article or division new chapters may be included by using one of the reserved chapter numbers care should be taken that the alphabetical arrangement of chapters is maintained when including new chapters page numbering system the page numbering system used in this a prefix system the letters to the left of the colon are an abbreviation which represents a certain portion of the volume the number to the right of the colon represents the number of the page in that portion in the case of a chapter of the the number to the left of the colon indicates the number of the chapter in the case of an appendix to the the letter immediately to the left of the colon indicates the letter of the appendix the following are typical parts of codes of ordinances which may or may not appear in this this time and their corresponding prefixes charter cht1 related laws rl1 special acts sa1 charter comparative table chtct1 related laws comparative table rlct1 special acts comparative table sact1 code cd code appendix cda1 code comparative tables cct1 state law reference table slt1 charter index chti1 code index cdi1 index the index has been prepared with the greatest of care each particular item has been placed under several headings some of which are couched in lay phraseology others in legal terminology and still others in language generally used by local government officials and employees there are numerous cross references within the index itself which stand as guideposts to direct the user to the particular item in which the user is interested looseleaf supplements a special feature of this publication is the looseleaf system of binding and supplemental servicing of the publication with this system the publication will be kept up to date subsequent amendatory legislation will be properly edited and the affected page or pages will be reprinted these new pages will be distributed to holders of copies of the publication with instructions for the manner of inserting the new pages and deleting the obsolete pages keeping this publication up to date at all times will depend largely upon the holder of the publication as revised pages are received it will then become the responsibility of the holder to have the amendments inserted according to the attached instructions it is strongly recommended by the publisher that all such amendments be inserted immediately upon receipt to avoid misplacing them and in addition that all deleted pages be saved and filed for historical reference purposes acknowledgments this publication was under the direct supervision of daniel walker kellyn wilcox editor of the municipal tallahassee florida credit is gratefully given to the other members of the publishers staff for their sincere interest and able assistance throughout the project the publisher is most grateful to mr shawn bell city administrator for his cooperation and assistance during the progress of the work on this publication it is hoped that his efforts those of others in the city administration and those of the publisher have resulted in a ordinances which will make the active law of the city readily accessible to all citizens and which will be a valuable tool in the prescribe copies thereof shall be distributed as determined by the city clerk 4 definitions for the purpose of this in the interpretation and application of all other ordinances heretofore or hereafter adopted except as the context may otherwise require city  the term city means the city of lake city in the county of florence and state of south carolina clerk or city clerk  the term clerk or city clerk means the municipal clerk duly elected pursuant to law council or city council  the term council or city council means the council of the city of lake city south carolina county  the term county means the county of florence state of south carolina department  the term department means an organizational unit of the government established or designated by ordinance or this a department together with any agency or instrumentality of the government assigned to such organizational unit by the city council laws  the term laws means laws of the state of south carolina licensed  the term licensed means licensed in accordance with the appropriate section or chapter of this  the term month means a calendar month oath  the term oath means and shall be construed to include an affirmation in all cases in which by law an affirmation may be substituted for an oath and in such cases the terms swear and sworn shall be equivalent to the terms affirm and affirmed the term ordinance means any act of local legislation heretofore or hereafter adopted and including this revision so long as it is adopted by the procedure required for the adoption of an ordinance and so long as it remains in force and effect pursuant to law owner  the term owner applied to a building or land means and includes any partowner joint owner tenant in common joint tenant or tenant by the entirety of the whole or part of such building or land person  the term person means any individual natural persons partnerships joint ventures societies associations clubs trustees trusts corporations or unincorporated groups  or any officers agents employees servants factors of any kind of personal representatives of any thereof in any capacity acting either for himself or for any other person under either personal appointment or pursuant to law personal property  the term personal property means and includes every species of property except real property as defined in this section property  the term property means and includes real and personal property real property and real estate  the terms real property and real estate mean and include lands tenements and hereditaments roadway  the term roadway means that portion of a street improved designed or ordinarily used for vehicular travel sc the term sc  means the laws of south carolina 197 as it may be amended or recodified from time to time sidewalk the term sidewalk means any portion of a street between the curbline or the lateral lines of a roadway where there is no curb and the adjacent property line intended for the use of pedestrians excluding parkways signature or subscription  the term signature or subscription means and includes a mark when a person cannot write state or this state  the term state or this state shall be construed to mean the state of south carolina street  the term street includes avenues boulevards highways roads alleys lanes viaducts bridges and approaches thereto and all other public thoroughfares in the city and shall mean the entire width thereof between abutting property lines a street shall be construed to include a sidewalk or footpath unless the contrary is expressed or unless such construction would be inconsistent with the manifest intent of the city council tenant or occupant  the term tenant or occupant when applied to a building or land means and includes any who occupies the whole or part of such building or land whether alone or with others year  the term year means a calendar year    15 construction a definitions for the purpose of this any other ordinances heretofore or hereafter adopted the following definitions and rules of construction shall be observed unless inconsistent with the manifest intent of the city council or the context clearly requires otherwise b in general andor the term and may be read as or and the term or may be read as and where the sense requires it bond when bond is required an undertaking in writing shall be sufficient computation of time the time within which an act is to be done shall be computed by excluding the first day and including the last and if the last day is a sunday or a legal holiday that shall be excluded preceding and following the terms preceding and following mean the next before and the next after respectively shallmay the term shall is mandatory and the term may is permissive generally 1 the present tense includes the past future tenses and the future the present 2 the masculine gender includes the feminine and neuter 3 the singular number includes the plural and the plural the singular 4 whenever a specific time is used in this revision it shall mean the prevailing and established time in effect in the state of south carolina during any day in any year 5 any citation of a statute law or ordinance contained in this revision shall be deemed to refer to such statute law or ordinance as amended whether or not such designation is included in the citation 6 all words giving a joint authority to three or more persons or officers shall be construed as giving such authority to a majority of such persons or officers d division of the means one of the major declared to be unconstitutional invalid or inoperative in whole or in part by a court of competent jurisdiction such chapter section subsection or paragraph shall to the extent that it is not unconstitutional invalid or inoperative remain in full force and effect and no such determination shall be deemed to invalidate the remaining chapters sections subsections or paragraphs of this    general penalty whenever in this in any ordinance or resolution of the city or rule regulation or order promulgated by any officer or agency of the city under authority duly vested in him or it any act is prohibited or is made or declared to be unlawful or an offense or misdemeanor or the doing of any act is required or the failure to do any act is declared to be unlawful or an offense or misdemeanor where no specific penalty is provided for the violation thereof the violation of such provisions of this ordinance resolution rule regulation or order shall be punished by a fine not exceeding $50000 or by imprisonment for a period not exceeding 30 days  provided however that no penalty shall exceed the penalty provided by the state law for similar offenses each day any violation of this any such ordinance rule or regulation shall continue shall constitute a separate offense 1   110   liability of corporations andor agents for violations any violation of this any officer agent or other person acting for or employed by any corporation or unincorporated association or organization while acting within the scope of his office or employment shall in every case also be deemed to be a violation by such corporation association or organization the individual shall be subject and liable to punishment as well as such corporation or unincorporated association or organization for the violation by it of any provision of this where such violation was the act or omission or the result of the act omission or order of any such person 2   111 uniform ordinance summons for violations a any person or entity violating any provisions of this any code adopted pursuant thereto within the corporate limits of the city may be issued a uniform ordinance issuance of the uniform ordinance summons shall vest jurisdiction in the municipal court to hear and dispose of the charge for which the uniform ordinance summons was issued and served the uniform ordinance summons may be issued by any city law enforcement officer or any other city employees designated by the council as code enforcement officers the bond amount for violations shall be prescribed by the municipal court judge city law enforcement or code enforcement officers are prohibited from accepting bonds bonds are to be posted in the manner prescribed in the uniform ordinance summons the uniform ordinance summons shall not be used to perform a custodial arrest b this section does not apply to any ordinance which regulates the use of motor vehicles on the public roads 3 fiscal year the fiscal year for the city shall commence on july 1 in each year and end on the following june 30 1   120 seal of the city the seal of the city is described as follows 1 within the outer circle is engraved city of lake city and in the middle circle the word seal is engraved 2 such seal is hereby established and declared to be the common seal of the city 3 the city clerk shall have the custody of the seal and it shall be kept by policies and procedures which are embodied in the municipal charter in statutory law or in city ordinances 1   2120 administrative regulations administrative regulations shall be issued by the mayor 2   2121 fee for collection of delinquent debts a the city hereby imposes an administrative fee as set forth in appendix a to the citys ordinances and as it may be amended by the city council from time to time to defray its internal costs of collection for any delinquent debts that are sought to be collected pursuant to the provisions of the setoff debt collection act sc  et seq this fee is hereby declared to be a collection cost that arises by operation of law and shall be added to the delinquent debt and recovered from the debtor b the city hereby declares that the administrative fee charged by the municipal association of south carolina is also a collection cost to the city which shall also be added to the delinquent debt and recovered from the debtor  2 11122013 secs 24224  reserved article ii  mayor division 1  generally chief administrative officer the mayor shall be the chief executive officer of the city and shall exercise all powers and authority vested in him by the city charter and ordinances and the law of the state in addition to the powers and duties exercised and required by him by law or ordinance it shall be his duty to be vigilant and active at all times in causing the ordinances and laws for the government of the city to be duly executed and put into force to inspect the conduct of all subordinate officers in the government or management of their respective offices and as far as is in his power to cause all negligence carelessness and positive violation of duty to be duly prosecuted and punished the mayor shall be considered city administrator for council until such time as a city administrator is provided 1   2130 state law reference responsibilities and duties of mayor sc  power to call council meetings the mayor shall have the power to call meetings of council for the transaction of business of the city whenever he may deem it necessary 2   2131 power to vote the mayor shall have a vote as member of council on all matters presented to council 3   2133 authority relative to city officers generally the mayor shall have full power to give such orders and directions to the executive officers of the city as may be necessary to carry out the provision of this other ordinances and regulations of the city and require them to attend meetings for that purpose at any time whenever the public business may in his opinion render such attendance necessary 4   2134 preparation of annual budget the mayor shall be responsible for the preparation of the budget annually with recommendations from the various departments of the city the mayor shall submit the annual budget to council and be responsible for its administration after adoption 5   2135 preparation of reports  financial accounting the mayor shall prepare or have prepared and submit to the council at the end of each fiscal year a complete annual report on the finances and administrative activities of the city for the preceding year  and make such other financial reports from time to time as may be required by council the mayor shall provide for a complete financial accounting to be made at the end of his term of office for presentation to the incoming administration 6   2136 investigation of city books papers and records the mayor shall have full power to investigate the books papers and records of the officers of the city whenever in his opinion it may be necessary or appoint others to do so 7   2137 devolution of powers and duties when mayor absent  mayor pro tem at the first meeting after inauguration council shall elect one of its members as mayor pro tem of the city the mayor pro tem shall be vested with all the powers duties and responsibilities of the office of mayor during the temporary absence or disability of the mayor or when the office of mayor shall be vacated by reason of death resignation removal or permanent disability of the mayor until such time as a new mayor shall have been elected and qualified in the absence or inability to act of both the mayor and the mayor pro tem the duties of the mayor shall devolve on and be performed by such councilmember as the council shall name 8   2138 secs 233252  reserved division 2  emergency powers of the mayor definitions the following words terms and phrases when used in this division shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning state of emergency shall be deemed to exist whenever during times of great public crisis disaster rioting civil disturbance catastrophe or for any other reason municipal public safety authorities are unable to maintain public order or afford adequate protection for lives safety health welfare or property 1   2150 power to impose regulations by proclamation whenever the mayor or the mayor pro tem in the event of the mayors inability to act determine that an emergency exists as a result of mob action or other civil disobedience causing danger or injury to or damages to persons or property he shall have power conditional upon a gubernatorial declaration to impose by proclamation any or all of the regulations contained within this section necessary to preserve the peace and order of the city 2   2151 power to impose curfew  persons exempt the mayor may order a curfew imposed upon all or any portion of the city thereby requiring all persons in such designated curfew areas to forthwith remove themselves from the public streets alleys parks or other public places  provided however that physicians nurses and ambulance operators performing medical services utility personnel maintaining essential public services firefighters and city authorized or requested law enforcement officers and personnel may be exempted from such curfew 3   2152 power to close areas to traffic the mayor may designate any public street thoroughfare or vehicle parking areas closed to motor vehicles and pedestrian traffic 5   2154 power to call in law enforcement the mayor may call upon regular and auxiliary law enforcement agencies and organizations within or without the city to assist in preserving and keeping the peace within the city 6   2155 proclamation of emergencyeffective the proclamation of emergency provided herein shall become effective upon its issuance and dissemination to the public by appropriate news media 7   2156 sametermination any emergency proclaimed in accordance with the provisions of this division shall terminate after 48 hours from the issuance thereof or upon the issuance of a proclamation determining an emergency no longer exists whichever occurs first  provided however that such emergency may be extended for such additional periods of time as determined necessary by resolution of the city council 8   2157 violation of proclamation  penalty any person who shall willfully fail or refuse to comply with the orders of duly authorized law enforcement officers or personnel charged with the responsibility of enforcing the proclamation of emergency authorized herein shall be deemed guilty of a misdemeanor and upon conviction therefor shall be liable to the penalty stated in section 18 9   2158 transfer of law enforcement officers to another municipality the mayor or council may upon the request of the governing body or mayor of any other municipality of the state send any law enforcement officer or officers to assist the law enforcement officers of such requesting municipality in the performance of their duties in cases of emergency a complete record of the request together with the names of the officers sent shall be recorded in the minutes of the next regular meeting of the governing bodies of the council such assistance shall be rendered only in emergencies and such emergency shall be declared by the mayor of the requesting city or town or in his absence the person normally acting in his stead 10   2159 rights powers duties of such officers law enforcement officers sent to another municipality pursuant to this division shall retain the jurisdiction authority rights privileges and immunities including coverage under workmens compensation laws which they now have and these shall be extended to and include the area in which like benefits and authorities are or could be afforded and the area between the two municipalities when acting within the scope of the authority to make arrests and to execute criminal process as is vested by law in the law enforcement officers of the requesting municipality and of no other 11   2160 model of proclamation i ___________ mayor of the city of lake city by virtue of the power vested in me by the provisions of of the ordinances of the city of lake city do hereby declare and determine that due to mob action and civil disobedience a state of emergency exists within the city of lake city and i do hereby order and direct the following emergency regulations to be effective immediately to wit 1 a curfew is hereby ordered from ___ oclock for the area located ___________ or for entire city and all persons other than law enforcement officers and personnel firemen physicians nurses ambulance operators performing medical services and utility personnel maintaining essential public services shall remain off the streets and away from public places during the period of the curfew 2 the following businesses are hereby ordered closed a taverns b retail and wholesale liquor establishments c gasoline service stations d any establishment selling firearms or ammunition e other designated businesses 3 all regular and auxiliary police and firemen are hereby ordered to report for duty immediately this proclamation shall be effective immediately and shall extend for a period of 48 hours date and time ___________ _____ mayor 12   2161 secs 264284  reserved article iii  establishment of city council division 1  generally form of city government  composition of council a the city does hereby select the mayorcouncil form of city government as required by sc  et seq b the governing body of the city shall consist of a mayor and six councilmembers and shall be known as the city council 1   21   inauguration and tenure the mayor and councilmembers shall take office on january 1 following their election and shall remain in office for a tenure of four years 2   compensation for mayor and councilmembers a the mayor and councilmembers may determine the annual salary of mayor and councilmembers by ordinance  provided that an ordinance establishing or increasing the salaries must not become effective until the commencement date of the terms of two or more members elected at the next general election following the adoption of the ordinance at that time it becomes effective for all members whether or not they were elected in that election b an ordinance reducing the salary of mayor and councilmembers is effective on the date the ordinance receives final reading unless provided otherwise c the mayor and councilmembers also may receive payment for actual expenses incurred in the performance of their official duties within limitations prescribed by ordinance 3   23   vacancies if a vacancy occurs in the office of mayor or councilmember an election to fill the vacancy shall be held in the same manner and after the same notice as provided in chapter 10 in the case that the vacancy should occur within 60 days before the regular election it shall be in the discretion of the city council whether or not an election is to be held to fill the vacancy 4   24 bond of city council the city council shall fix a bond for the members of the council to ensure the faithful performance of their duties 5   25 financial statement of council the members of the city council shall publish at the end of each year a full statement of their receipts and expenditures during the preceding year the members of council shall within 30 days after the expiration of their term and at such time as their successors have been qualified make and deliver to the newly elected members a full and accurate account of the receipts and expenditures during the term for which they were elected 6   26 delivery of items to successors at the end of their term the members of the city council shall pay over to their successors any sum of money that they may have in their hands or have control of at the time of making the statement required by section 290 the councilmembers shall also deliver at the end of their term all books records or other property incident to their offices to their successors 7   27 liability for negligence the mayor or councilmembers shall be liable to the penalty stated in section 18 in addition to damages to any person injured for any willful violation or neglect of duty so certified by this section who shall be as follows 1 all permanent improvements or capital investments shall be authorized only by vote of the city council 2 all current bills and operating expenses over $500000 shall be approved by the mayor and city council prior to payment by the director of finance each payment must be within the budget appropriation of that department and payment over that budgetary limit must be approved by city council 3 city administrator has the authority to approve on expenditures up to $500000 any expense over this amount must be approved by the mayor and council 4 all special subscriptions and donations by the city must be approved by the city council 3   222   city officers the city council may appoint a clerk auditor city attorney judge who shall not be the next meeting regular or special of the city council and his action shall be subject to review by and action of the city council 5   225 powers to investigate  subpoena witnesses the city council has to compel the attendance of witnesses and to require them to give evidence under oath in the same manner as in the courts of this state 6   226 power to hold in contempt  certain actions a any for similar offenses in the courts of this state b it shall be unlawful for any person to annoy disturb or interfere with any session or meeting of the mayor and councilmembers in council assembled by any means or any manner or to use profane obscene or disrespectful language gestures or signs to or in the presence thereof or to commit any offense which is by the laws of this state deemed a contempt 7   227 appeal from administrative rules and regulations a every citizen who shall be held to be in violation of any rule regulation or directive of the city normal governmental operation shall have recourse by appeal to the city council except for those violations normally handled by the court b to perfect this appeal the petitioner must reduce it to writing by citing the violation date and time and all the facts bearing thereon as he sees them and present it to council or to the clerk of the city for transmittal to the council at their session next c council shall have the right to deny the petition or to alter amend or rescind the rule regulation or directive as their investigation shall advise 8   228 secs 21212138  reserved division 3  responsibilities of city meeting to preside until the mayor or mayor pro tem appears the presiding officer shall preserve decorum and shall decide all questions of order subject to appeal to the council 7   260 interested responsibilities is required to take an action or make a decision which affects an economic interest of himself a family member an individual with whom he is associated or a business with which he is associated shall 1 prepare a written statement describing the matter requiring action or decisions and the nature of his potential conflict of interest with respect to the action or decision  2 furnish a copy of the statement to the mayor or the mayor shall furnish a copy of the statement to the mayor pro tem who shall cause the statement to be printed in the minutes and require that the member of council or the mayor shall be excused from any votes deliberations and other actions on the matter on which the potential conflict of interest exists and shall cause the disqualification and duties punishment for the violation hereof shall be as stated in chapter 18 article i 5   2175 random drug testing a all persons applying for employment with the city shall be subject to having a urinalysis the urinalysis shall be monitored by appropriate medical personnel who take the sample the sample shall be maintained by the medical personnel until the sample is transported to the laboratory for testing there shall be a record of the chain of custody of the sample from the time of taking the sample until delivery of the sample to the laboratory maintained by the medical personnel administering the test the test results shall be returned to the physician who shall in turn forward the results to the chief administrative assistant b no applicant testing positive for unlawful drugs shall be employed by the city c every employee of the city shall be subject to a urinalysis on a random basis samples for testing shall be obtained in a reasonable manner so that it will not cause an undue hardship on any employee all samples shall be monitored and the chain of custody documented to the laboratory making the test to ensure confidentially all test results are to be forwarded from the laboratory to the chief administrative assistant d any employee failing to report for testing or refusing to be tested shall be subject to disciplinary action including termination e any employee may have his employment with the city terminated if he tests positive for unlawful drugs or at the option of the mayor the employee may be allowed the benefit of section 16354c the disciplinary action of the city shall not be subject to appeal by the employee f procedures 1 a private sterile environment shall be used by the employee to provide his sample 2 the physician or his designated representative shall dispense sterile containers to the employee for a urine sample 3 to ensure originality of a sample only one employee will be tested at a time 4 to ensure originality of a sample food coloring or dye shall be placed in the commode where samples are provided by the employee 5 to ensure confidentiality sample bottles will be numbered the name of the employee will not be used on the sample bottle as a means of identification 6 a record of the number assigned to the employee will be maintained by the physician or his designated representative or the record of name and number may be given to the chief administrative assistant 7 a local professional medical laboratory when a qualified local laboratory is available shall process all drug screens for the city 6   secs 23402366  reserved article x  municipal court footnotes  2  editors note the municipal court may 1 under sc  try and determine criminal cases involving violations of article ii  regulations concerning animals and fowl animals and fowl prohibited at large  exceptions it shall be unlawful for any person to permit suffer or let whether by negligence carelessness or otherwise any animal to run at large within the corporate limits of the city  provided however that this article shall not apply to dogs it shall be the duty of the police officers to seize and secure any animal or fowl that may be found running at large and to impound the same in an enclosure provided for that purpose it shall be lawful for any person residing in the city or any employee of the city to seize any such animal or fowl running at large within the city and deliver the same to a police officer to be impounded as provided for in this article 1   52 notice of impoundment  reclamation not later than 24 hours after the impounding of any animal the owner if known shall be notified the owner of any animal so impounded may reclaim such animal upon payment of all notices of violation outstanding against the owner 2    amended by florence county ordinances  62 disposition of unclaimed or infected animals it shall be the duty of the animal control officer to keep all animals so impounded for a period not exceeding 21 days  provided however that unvaccinated animals whose owners are unknown may be sold or disposed of by a humane form of execution if such animal remains unclaimed for three days after 21 days such animal may be released to a medical college or other research organization humanely destroyed or sold any animal which appears to be suffering from rabies hydrophobia mange or other infectious or dangerous disease shall not be released but shall be put to sleep 3    amended by florence county ordinances  63 rescuing animals from the pound it shall be unlawful for any person to rescue attempt to rescue or take away from the pound any animal unless the charges due on such animal have been paid 4   55 keeping domestic animals within the city it shall be unlawful for any person to keep maintain or have in his possession within the city any hogs pigs calves or cows horses ponies mules or burros  provided that this section shall not apply to such businesses as provided by section 430 or to a mere temporary keeping or having in possession of such animals as an incident to their immediate slaughter for personal use or passage of such animals city or shipment therefrom nor shall this section apply to fairs parades contests or like exhibitions when licensed or permitted by the city and in conformity with such sanitation regulation as may be required by the health officer in connection therewith 5   56 poultry within the city it shall be unlawful to keep or maintain any poultry within the city except in such buildings structures enclosures or upon such grounds as are kept in sanitary condition including provisions of suitable and proper drainage and precautions against breeding of flies  provided that such poultry house or poultry yard is at least a distance of 30 feet from any dwelling house 6   57 wild animals within the city  exceptions a it shall be unlawful for any person to keep maintain or have in his possession within the city any deer bears foxes monkeys or other wild animals caged or uncaged  provided that this section shall not apply to a mere temporary keeping or having in possession of such animals as an incident to the passage of such animals city or shipment therefrom the provisions of this section shall not apply to circuses menageries or like displays of animals for short intervals of time and under permit or license from the city b this section shall not apply to the keeping of small wild animals in the home or immediately adjacent thereto as pets  provided that such animals are kept securely caged or that they do not become a nuisance or annoyance to the neighborhood or a source of danger to the citizens of the community the code enforcement officer shall have the authority to determine whether the keeping of such animal as may be permitted by this section shall be unsanitary or detrimental to the health and welfare of the community upon determination that such condition exists the further keeping or the animal shall be unlawful 7   58 permits required for stables or like businesses it shall be unlawful for any person to open maintain keep or conduct any stable or place of business where animals are sold offered for sale exchanged or kept for hire without first applying to and obtaining from the city council a permit to operate such business the application for such permit shall be in writing and shall set forth fully the location the nature probable volume of the business to be conducted and the precautions to be taken by the applicant against having such business offensive to the public health peace and safety the city council may grant or refuse such permits in its discretion or attach any conditions to the grant any permit shall be subject to revocation in the discretion of the city council or the imposition of further conditions if the public welfare requires no permit shall be revoked or made subject to further conditions except upon notice to the holder of the permit and opportunity granted to him to be heard by the city council on the question involved the city council may also in its discretion remove any or all of the conditions attached to the grant of such permit 8   59 unhitched horses on streets it shall be unlawful for any person to leave any horse or other draft animal on the streets of the city unless the animal is in some manner securely fastened 9   510 driving animals at dangerous speeds  reckless riding it shall be unlawful for any person to drive horses or other animals at a dangerous rate of speed in the city or in such manner as to endanger persons on the streets 10   511 driving leading animals on sidewalks it shall be unlawful for any person to lead or drive any animal on or along any sidewalk in the city except directly across the same from or to the street for the purpose of crossing the same  provided however that the provisions of this section shall not apply to dogs 11   512 hitching animals to fences poles it shall be unlawful for any person to hitch any animal to any fences shade tree telegraph or telephone pole or lamp post 12   513 hitching animals near streets sidewalks public places it shall be unlawful for any person to hitch or tie any animal in such a way that the same may walk upon any sidewalk or public street or public place in the city  provided that this section shall not apply to the hitching or tying of dogs 13   514 sale of diseased animals it shall be unlawful for any person to sell or to offer for sale in the city any animal or poultry of any kind that is known to be affected with any contagious disease the tendency of which is to cause the death of such animal or fowl  and it shall be unlawful for any person to sell or to offer for sale any animal or fowl that may be used for human food that is sick or diseased in any manner at the time of sale without fully informing the purchaser of the nature and extent of such sickness or disease so far as the same comes within the sellers knowledge  nor shall any animal or fowl be sold or offered for sale within the city that has been exposed within a short time previous thereto to the knowledge of the seller to any contagious or other sickness or disease unless the seller shall fully inform the purchaser thereof so far as his knowledge extends 15   516 dead animals and poultry within city limits a whenever any animal or poultry shall die from any natural or other cause except from being slaughtered or killed for the use of man or the dead body thereof be found upon the premises of any person be he the owner or tenant thereof the owner of such dead animal or poultry or the owner or tenant of the lands or premises upon which the dead bodies may be found shall immediately and not later than 24 hours after discovery burn or bury or cause to be burned or buried such dead animal or poultry when buried the animal shall be put not less than three feet and poultry not less than one foot under the ground b any owner of any such animal or poultry or any tenant on premises having knowledge that such animal or poultry is lying dead on his premises and who refuses or fails to bury such dead animal or poultry as aforesaid upon conviction shall be liable to the penalty stated in section 18 16   517 hydrophobia glanders or farcy it shall be unlawful for any person to bring or keep within the city limits any horse or other animal having a disease known as glanders or farcy or any animal having a disease known as hydrophobia persons having an animal so affected shall forthwith report the same to the board of health along with the name of the owner and the place where the animal is left and appropriate action will be taken by the board 17   518 report of dead animals and fowl any person having upon his premises any dead animal or fowl shall immediately report such dead animal or fowl to the health officer 18   519 abattoirs within city limits it shall be unlawful to slaughter or butcher any bullock cow cattle sheep swine calves or goats within the city limits except at a duly licensed abattoir 19   520 secs 441468  reserved article county ordinances  65 duty of owner detecting rabies symptoms it shall be the duty of any person owning or having in his possession any dog or animal within the city which develops any symptoms of rabies to immediately notify the health officer or health department of such condition and to immediately confine the dog or animal securely in such a manner that there will be no opportunity for it to come into contact with other animals and keep it segregated and confined until notification by the health officer of proper disposition the dog shall be under the observation of a licensed veterinarian at the owners expense for a period of two weeks every owner or other person upon ascertaining that a dog is rabid shall immediately notify the poundmaster or health department who shall summarily destroy it 3   551 police authority when rabies suspected whenever a case or suspected case of rabies has occurred in the city the police department shall have the power and it shall be its duty to prevent the spread of the disease by ordering that all dogs or other domestic pets in the city shall be locked up restrained by a leash or muzzled or shall order all owners or keepers of same to take such preventive measures as the police department may deem necessary or both the department shall have the power within the city limits to destroy any rabid dog or any dog exhibiting the symptoms thereof the police department shall exercise this power subject to state law governing the duties of the county health department in like situations 4   552 failure to comply with police orders in the event any owner or keeper of any dog or domestic pet shall knowingly fail or refuse to comply with the order of the police department duly given under the authority of section 472 it shall be the prerogative of the police department to seize the dog and take whatever action it deems appropriate and which is not inconsistent with state law governing the duties of the county health department in like situations 5   553 duty of health officer to destroy rabid dogs when the health officer determines that any dog he has inspected has rabies or exhibits the symptoms of rabies it shall be his duty to kill or have killed such a dog  provided nothing contained herein shall be taken as an abridging or limiting the power of the police under existing law to kill on sight any dog in the city exhibiting symptoms of rabies it shall also be the duty of the health officer to destroy any dog that has been bitten or injured by a dog reliably identified as rabid or exhibiting the symptoms thereof 6   554 obstructing the health officer it shall be unlawful for any person to obstruct resist hinder or oppose the health officer of the city or any police officer or other person acting under his authority in carrying out the duties as prescribed by this article 7   555 secs 476493  reserved article iv  rabies control inoculations required a it shall be the duty of every person in the county owning or in the possession of a pet over four months of age to have such pet inoculated with an antirabic vaccine approved by the state health department which inoculation shall be repeated as often as the state board of health may from time to time specify  but in no case shall the recognized immunity of phenolized or brain tissue vaccine exceed one year and the chick embryo or modified live virus vaccine exceed three years the expense of inoculation of pets against rabies shall be borne by the owners of such pets such inoculations shall be made by a licensed graduate veterinarian who shall furnish a certificate of vaccination to the county health department animal control division within 30 days following vaccination on a form prepared and issued by the department of health and environmental control and no other certificate shall be used such certificate of vaccination shall be the only valid evidence of compliance with this article upon such vaccination the person issuing the certificate of vaccination shall also issue an immunity tag valid as long as the vaccination with reference to which it is issued is valid which shall be attached to the collar of the pet so vaccinated the provisions of this article shall be subject to the provisions of the state rabies control act and any and all amendments thereof b the health department shall require the owner of any dog or cat which has bitten or attacked a person to confine the pet for ten days during which the rabies control officer or animal control officer must be given access to the pet at any time to check for symptoms of rabies as prescribed by sc  if the bite or attack was perpetrated by a pet other than a dog or cat the owner shall have the animal euthanized immediately and have the brain submitted for rabies examination as prescribed by sc  c any animal known to have been bitten by an animal known or suspected of being affected by rabies shall be confined as required by the health department as prescribed by sc  1    amended by florence county ordinances  618 unvaccinated dogs prohibited  penalty a it shall be unlawful for any person to have an unvaccinated pet in the notice of violation  provided however that proof of the vaccination shall be accepted in lieu of the fine for the first offense c in the event that such penalty is not paid within the time prescribed a warrant shall be initiated by the animal control officer and upon conviction of a violation of this article the owner shall be fined not more than $10000 or imprisoned more than 30 days for each entirety to read as herein set out formerly article iii  655667 pertained to similar subject matter and derived from xiv145a1417 adopted  state law reference dwellings unfit for human habitation sc 3115120 purpose the city council finds that there exists within the city certain dwellings which are unfit for human habitation due to dilapidation  defects increasing the hazards of fire accidents or other calamities  lack of ventilation light or sanitary facilities  and other conditions rendering such dwellings unsafe or unsanitary dangerous or detrimental to the health safety or morals or otherwise inimical to the welfare of the residents of the city  892016 police powers of the city  appointment of building official whenever it is determined that any dwelling is found unfit or unsafe to occupy because any of the conditions exist as set forth in section 658 or because it does not meet the minimum requirements of the international property maintenance the police powers of the city may be exercised to cause the repair closure or demolition of any such dwelling in the manner hereinafter provided the building official of the city is hereby appointed and authorized to determine that a dwelling is unfit for human habitation upon a finding that the conditions set forth in section 658 exist  892016 building official  powers and duties in order to implement the provisions of this article the building official may exercise the following powers addition to other powers granted herein 1 to investigate the dwelling conditions in the city in order to determine which dwellings therein are unfit for human habitation  2 to administer oaths and affirmations examine witnesses and receive evidence with respect to the proceedings carried out pursuant to this article  3 to enter upon premises for the purpose of making examination provided such entries be made in a manner as to cause the least possible inconvenience to the persons in possession  and 4 with the approval of the city administrator to designate any other employee of the city to include the city administrator to carry out the provisions of this article and to appoint and fix the duties of such officers agents and employees of the city as deemed necessary to carry out the purposes of this article  892016 conditions constituting unfit dwellings a dwelling is unfit for human habitation if conditions exist in the dwelling which are dangerous or injurious to the health safety or morals of the occupants of the dwelling the occupants of neighboring dwellings or other residents of the city conditions making a dwelling unfit for human habitation may include the following without limiting the generality of the foregoing standard defects therein increasing the hazards of fire accidents or other calamities  lack of adequate ventilation light or sanitary facilities  dilapidation  disrepair  structural defects  uncleanliness  or any other conditions listed as unsafe conditions pursuant the international property maintenance as it may be amended or updated from time to time  892016 issuance of complaint a whenever a petition is filed with the building official by the mayor or his designee the city administrator or at least five residents of the city charging that any dwelling is unfit for human habitation or whenever it appears to the building official on his own motion that any dwelling is unfit for human habitation the building official shall conduct a preliminary investigation with respect to the fitness of the dwelling for human habitation in the event that the dwelling is found to unfit for human habitation the building official shall issue a complaint disclosing the basis for such charges and cause the complaint to be served upon the owner of and all parties in interest in the dwelling upon the issuance of the complaint the building official shall fix the time and place for a hearing which shall be held before the building official which shall not be less than ten days nor more than 30 days after the date of service of the complaint the owner and parties in interest shall be given the right to file an answer to the complaint at any time prior to the hearing and to appear in person or otherwise and give testimony at the hearing at the time and place set forth in the complaint b any complaint issued by the building official under this article shall 1 include a description of the real property that is the subject of the complaint sufficient to identify the property  2 include a statement of conditions that are believed to make the dwelling unfit for human habitation  3 include a notice that a hearing will be held before the building official or his designated representative along with the date time and place of such hearing  4 inform the owner of the right to answer the complaint at any time prior to the hearing  5 inform the owner of the right to give testimony at the hearing and the right to be represented at the hearing by any other party including an attorney  6 include a statement stating that if the conditions with respect to the dwelling are not remediated so as to make the dwelling fit for human habitation the building official may require the repair alteration or improvement or the demolition or removal of the dwelling  892016 conduct of hearing any hearing held pursuant to the provisions of this article shall be conducted using the following procedure 1 all hearings shall be conducted in an open session before the building official at the time and place set forth in the complaint the building official shall provide a summary of the conditions that are believed to make the dwelling unfit for human habitation the owner any party in interest or a representative of the owner or any party in interest which may be an attorney shall be permitted to respond 2 any hearing shall be recorded and copies thereof made available to the owner or any party in interest at no charge upon request 3 hearings shall not be subject to the rules of evidence but the building official may mandate that only relevant information be presented 4 the building official shall make a final determination of the action required of the owner if any that is necessary in order to make the dwelling fit for human habitation the building official may decide upon any such matter at the hearing or may take the matter under consideration to be decided upon at a later date the building official shall serve upon the owner an order stating the final determination of the building official as to the appropriate remedy pursuant to section 661 with respect to the dwelling and the findings of fact in support of such determination  892016 remedies where dwellings are unfit for human habitation a if the repair alteration or improvement of the dwelling can be made at a reasonable cost in relation to the value of the dwelling the owner shall be required within the time specified in such order to repair alter or improve such dwelling to render it fit for human habitation or if the owner is unwilling or unable to make such repairs alterations or improvements to vacate close and board up the dwelling as a human habitation b if the repair alteration or improvement of the dwelling cannot be made at a reasonable cost in relation to the value of the dwelling the owner then shall be required within the time specified in the order to remove or demolish such dwelling  892016 issuance of orders any order issued by the building official pursuant to this article shall 1 include a final determination as to whether the dwelling is unfit for human habitation including where a dwelling is found to be unfit for human habitation a recitation of the findings of fact that support such a determination  2 fix a time period during which the owner must take the remedial action necessary to correct the conditions that cause the dwelling to be unfit for human habitation or the time period during which the owner must demolish or remove the dwelling  3 include a statement informing the owner of the right to appeal the determination of the building official by filing a petition in the circuit court of the county in which the dwelling is situated for an injunction restraining the building official from carrying out the provisions of the order  and 4 notify the owner that in the event the action required by the order is not taken within the prescribed period of time set forth therein the city may undertake such remedial action and in the event that the city does so any costs of the city including legal costs that are not offset by the sale of salvage or valuable materials shall become a lien against the real property upon which the dwelling was situated that shall be collectible in the same manner as municipal taxes including foreclosure and the sale of the property at a tax sale  892016 rights of persons affected by orders any person affected by an order issued by the building official may within 60 days after the posting or service of the order petition the circuit court of the county in which the dwelling is situated for an injunction restraining the building official from carrying out the provisions of the order the remedies set forth in this section shall be exclusive remedies and no person affected by an order of the building official shall be entitled to recover any damages for such action taken pursuant to any order or because of compliance by the building official or any other employee or contractor of the city with any order of the building official  892016 closure of dwellings if the owner fails to timely comply with the order to repair alter or improve or to vacate board up and close the dwelling the building official may cause the dwelling to be repaired altered or improved or to be vacated boarded up and closed in such case the building official shall cause to be posted on the main entrance of any dwelling so closed a placard with the following words this building is unfit for human habitation  the use or occupation of this building for human habitation is prohibited and unlawful  892016 removal authority of city if the owner fails to timely comply with an order to remove or demolish the dwelling the building official may cause the dwelling to be removed or demolished in the event that the city employs a thirdparty contractor to demolish or remove the dwelling the city shall competitively bid the work in conformity with the citys procurement and purchasing policy  892016 disposition of proceeds of sale  recovery of costs a if a dwelling is repaired altered or improved or removed or demolished by the city pursuant to this article the building official shall sell the salvage or valuable materials from the demolition of the dwelling and shall credit the proceeds of such sale against the costs of the city related to the removal or demolition of the dwelling including any legal costs related thereto the balance remaining shall be deposited in the circuit court to be secured in the manner directed by the court and shall be disbursed to the persons found to be entitled thereto by final order or decree of the court b if the proceeds of the sale of the salvage or valuable materials from the demolition or removal of the dwelling do not fully offset the costs of the city related to the demolition or removal of the dwelling including any legal costs related thereto such costs shall become a lien against the real property upon which the dwelling was situated that shall be collectible in the same manner as municipal taxes  892016 service complaints orders or any other notices under this article shall be served upon owners or other parties in interest either personally provided the subject of such service signs a certificate of receipt or by registered mail if the whereabouts of such persons is unknown and cannot be ascertained in the exercise of reasonable diligence or if the owner refuses to accept receipt of registered mail the building official shall make an affidavit to that effect and the serving of such complaint order or notice upon such persons may be made by publishing it once each week for two consecutive weeks in a newspaper that circulates in the city a copy of such complaint order or notice shall be posted in a conspicuous place on the premises affected by the complaint order or notice a copy of such complaint or order shall also be filed with the clerk of court in the county in which the dwelling is situated and such filing of the complaint or order shall have the same force and effect as other lis pendens notices provided by law  892016 unlawful to remove or deface notice  trespassing a it shall be unlawful for any person to remove or deface any complaint order or notice placed upon any dwelling pursuant to the provisions of this article b it shall be unlawful for any person to trespass upon the property posted pursuant to section 664  892016 nuisance abatement power of city no part of this article vi  buildings partially or totally destroyed by fire duty of owner generally it shall be the duty of all persons owning real estate within the corporate limits of the city on which any building has been partially or totally destroyed by fire to remove the debris from the premises or to repair and put such building in a habitable condition 1   930 enforcement of article by fire chief  notice to remedy condition it shall be the duty of the chief of the fire department to enforce the provisions of this article he shall give notice in writing to the owner of the building damaged by fire which notice shall specify the location of the premises and shall direct the owner thereof within a period of four months from the date of such notice to comply with the terms of this article in cases of nonresidents of the city such notice shall be given by registered mail addressed to the owner at his last known address 2   931 duty of owner upon notice within four months after written notice from the chief of the fire department so to do it shall be the duty of every owner of real estate on which there is situated any remains of any building partially or totally destroyed by fire to repair such building and place it in a habitable condition unless prohibited by the zoning ordinance or to remove such portion of the building and the trash and burned portion thereof from the premises and put the premises in a clean condition 3   932 noncompliance in the event any owner shall fail to comply with the provisions of this article or with the terms of the notice as provided by section 6152 the chief of the fire department is hereby authorized to enter upon the premises with such assistance as may be necessary and to remove the debris or remains of any building damaged by fire as specified in the notice upon the completion of the work the chief shall report to the city finance director the cost thereof which cost shall be charged against the defaulting owner and the finance director shall forthwith demand the payment of the same in the case of nonresidents the finance director may make demand for payment of costs by registered mail in the event such cost is not paid within five days after demand the city finance director shall issue his execution directed to the tax collector of the city who shall forthwith proceed to levy upon and sell any of the property real or personal of such owner so in default sufficient to pay all charges and costs in such cases the tax collector shall be entitled to collect the same costs as are now provided by law on tax article is for the purpose of providing such regulation as may be required by the businesses subject thereto and for the purpose of raising revenue for the general fund privilege excise tax each license shall be issued for one year and shall expire on december 31 the renewal of the business license will begin on the january 2 following the expiration date or the first working day thereafter the provisions of this article and the rates herein shall remain in effect from year to year as amended by city council        12122017 license excise fee the required license excise fee shall be paid for each business subject hereto by the due date the license excise fee shall be calculated according to the applicable rate classification in effect as of december 30 of the immediately preceding year a separate license shall be required for each place of business and for each classification or business conducted at one place if gross income cannot be separated for classifications at one location the license excise fee shall be computed on the combined gross income for the classification requiring the highest rate a license excise tax based on gross income shall be computed on the gross income for the preceding calendar or fiscal year and on a 12month projected income based on the monthly average for a business in operation for less than one year the excise tax for a new business shall be computed on the estimated probable gross income stated in the license application for the balance of the license year        12122017 registration required the owner agent or legal shall contain the social security number andor the federal employers identification number the business name as reported on the state income excise tax return and all information about the applicant and the business deemed necessary to carry out the purposes of this article by the license inspector the applicant shall certify under oath that the information given in the application is true that the gross income is accurately reported or estimated for a new business without any unauthorized deductions and that all assessments and personal property excise taxes due and payable to the city have been paid insurance agents and brokers shall report the name of each insurance company for which a policy was issued and the total premiums collected for each company for each type of insurance income shall be made except income from business done wholly outside of the city on which a license excise tax is paid to some other municipality or a county or income which cannot be taxed pursuant to state or federal law the applicant shall have the burden to establish the right to deduction by satisfactory records and proof b no person shall be exempt from the requirements of this article by reason of the lack of an established place of business within the city unless exempted by state or federal law the license inspector shall determine the appropriate classification for each business in accordance with the latest issue of the us office of management and budget standard industrial classification manual or the naics north american industry classification manual no person shall be exempt from this article by reason of the payment of any other excise tax unless exempted by state law and no person shall be relieved of the liability for the payment of any other excise tax by reason of the application of this article c charitable organizations which have exemptions from state and federal income excise taxes shall be exempt from a business license excise tax only in cases where the sponsors organizers directors trustees or persons who exercise ultimate control of the organization receive no part of the proceeds of operation and all proceeds are devoted to charitable purposes as defined by this article payment of necessary costs of operation and wages to nonmanagement employees will not disqualify a charitable organization from exemption d any person who is involved in leasing i four or fewer residential dwelling units or ii three or fewer nonresidential units or a combination of residential and nonresidential units each of which is owned by such person shall not be included within the definition of a business for the purposes of this article and shall be exempt from any license excise tax imposed pursuant to this article any person leasing property in numbers in excess of the thresholds established hereby shall be included within the definition of a business and subject to a license excise tax as to the entirety of the property leasing activities of such person      1182016   12122017 false application unlawful it shall be unlawful for any person subject to the provisions of this article to make a false application for a business license or to give or file or direct the giving or filing of any false information with respect to the license or excise fee required by this article      12122017 display and transfer all persons shall display the license issued to them on the original form provided by the license inspector in a conspicuous place in the business establishment at the address shown on the license a transient or the license inspector within ten days after removal of the business to a new location and the license will be valid at the new address upon written notification of the license inspector and compliance with zoning and building codes failure to obtain the approval of the license inspector for a change of address shall invalidate the license and subject the licensee to prosecution for doing business without a license a business license shall not be transferable and a transfer of ownership shall be considered a termination of the old business and the establishment of a new business requiring a new information has been filed by the licensee the costs of the audit shall be added to the correct license excise fee and late penalties in addition to other penalties provided herein each day of failure investigations and statistical surveys as he may deem appropriate to assess a license excise tax and penalties as provided herein a notice of assessment shall be served by certified mail and an application for adjustment of the assessment may be made to the license inspector within five days after the notice is mailed or the assessment will become final the license inspector shall establish      12122017 delinquent license excise fees for nonpayment of all or any part of the correct license excise fee by the due date the license inspector shall levy and collect a late penalty of five denial shall be written with reasons stated    suspension or revocation of license when the license inspector determines that 1 a license has been mistakenly or improperly issued or issued contrary to law  2 a licensee has breached any condition upon which his license was issued or has failed to comply with the provisions of this article  3 a licensee has obtained a license fraud misrepresentation a false or misleading statement evasion or suppression of a material fact in the license application  4 a licensee has been convicted of an offense under a law or ordinance regulating business a crime involving moral turpitude or an unlawful sale of merchandise or prohibited goods  or 5 a licensee has engaged in an unlawful activity or nuisance related to the business  the license inspector shall give written notice to the licensee or the person in control of the business within the city by personal service or certified mail that the license is suspended pending a hearing before city council for the purpose of determining whether the license should be revoked the notice shall state the time and place at which the hearing is to be held which shall be at a regular or special council meeting within 30 days from the date of service of the notice the notice shall contain a brief statement of the reasons for suspension and proposed revocation and a copy of the applicable provisions of this article    appeals to city council a any person aggrieved by a final assessment or a denial of a business license by the license inspector may appeal the decision to city council by written request stating the reasons therefor filed with the license inspector within ten days after the payment of the assessment under protest or notice of denial is received b an appeal or a hearing on revocation shall be held by city council within 30 days after receipt of a request for appeal or service of notice of suspension at a regular or special meeting of which the applicant or licensee has been given written notice at such hearing all parties shall have the right to be represented by counsel to present testimony and evidence and to cross examine witnesses the proceedings shall be recorded and transcribed at the expense of the party so requesting the rules of evidence and procedure prescribed by council shall govern the hearing city council shall by majority vote of members present render a written decision based on findings of fact and the application of the standards herein which shall be served upon all parties or their representatives and shall be final unless appealed to a court of competent jurisdiction within ten days after service c no person shall be subject to a prosecution for doing business without a license until the expiration of ten days after notice of denial or revocation which is not appealed or until after final judgment of a circuit court upholding denial or revocation    confidentiality except in accordance with proper judicial order or as otherwise pursuant to sc  the mayor shall be elected at large and councilmembers shall be elected one member from each ward of the municipality by the qualified electors of the ward as shown on lake city council district plan 1 candidates seeking office from a particular ward shall be residents of the ward during their entire term of office  terms of office the office of mayor shall be for the term of four years and the office of council shall be for the term of four years staggered  nonpartisan plurality method of elections all regular and special elections for mayor and councilmembers should be conducted and results shall be determined in accordance with the nonpartisan plurality method authorized by sc  as follows 1 when more than one person is seeking election to a single office the majority shall be ascertained by dividing the total votes cast for all candidates by two any excess of the sum so ascertained shall be a majority and the candidate who obtains a majority shall be declared elected 2 when more persons are seeking election to two or more offices constituting a group than there are offices to be filled the majority shall be ascertained by dividing the total votes cast for all candidates by the number of offices to be filled and by dividing the result by two any excess of the sum so ascertained shall be a majority and the candidates who obtain a majority shall be declared elected if more candidates obtain a majority than there are offices to be filled those having the highest vote equal to the number of offices to be filled shall be declared elected a if no candidate for single office receives a majority of the votes cast in the first election or if an insufficient number of candidates receives a majority of the votes cast for a group of offices a runoff election shall be held as herein provided b if no candidate for a single office receives a majority of the votes cast in the first election a second election shall be conducted two weeks later between the two candidates receiving the largest number of votes in the first election who do not withdraw the candidate receiving a majority of the votes cast in the runoff election shall be declared elected c if candidates for two or more offices constituting a group are to be selected and aspirants for some or all of the positions within the group do not receive a majority of the votes cast in the first election a second election shall be conducted two weeks later between one or more than the number of candidates necessary to fill the vacant offices the candidates receiving the highest number of the votes cast in the second election equal in number to be elected shall be declared elected  elections conducted by municipal election commission all regular and special elections shall be conducted by a municipal election commission composed of three electors who shall be residents of the city appointed by the city council for terms of six years staggered so that the terms of one member expires each evennumbered year at least 90 days prior to the regular election the election commission shall have the powers and duties specified in sc  and applicable provisions of title 7 of the south carolina  dates of elections regular elections for the office of mayor and members of council shall be held in even numbered years on the first tuesday after the first monday in november in the event of a tie vote for any office a runoff election shall be held two weeks following the election pursuant sc  special elections to fill vacancies shall be held pursuant to sc  two public notices of a regular or special election shall be given which shall include the location of polling places the first notice shall be given at least 60 days prior to the election and the second notice shall be i  in general enforcement of code and permits the international fire by the state building code council shall be enforced by the chief of the fire department subject to such rules and regulations as
